[20/01/19, 5:27:05 PM] Akhil Mohan (pushstart): Hello Everyone, I am working on a small tool to print Bank Statement (Savings as well as Current) online. Are there any free/paid APIs (Bank as well as third Party) that would allow access to customer's Bank Statement in CSV format (any other format will also work). At this moment, I am trying to connect with ICICI, HDFC and Kotak. Anyone here who has knowledge of such integrations or can put me in touch with a person who has worked on such a tech.

I guess there must be some sort of eligibility criteria for Banks to allow such integrations. Can anyone point me to eligibility criteria for ICICI, HDFC and Kotak.
[20/01/19, 6:30:19 PM] Ashutosh Vyas (pushstart): There are 2 ways to it.


1. Like other accounting apps (wave, zoho etc) have a read only access to your accounts. They can read your transactions but cannot execute any. These APIs are provided by the banks.


2. Some apps like the new Cred read your emails with bank account statements and fetch details from there. This is easier to get started bt technically could be a challange.
[20/01/19, 6:34:49 PM] Akhil Mohan (pushstart): With Zoho, the biggest problem is their uptime. They themselves depend on Yoodle and many times do not have clue why their integration with a particular bank is facing problem. I will check wave if they support Indian accounts.

Reading emails is a good idea, quite similar to accessing sms etc but I am also interested in authenticity of data as we wish to print statement. Thru emails etc we might not be always sure about source.

[05/02/19, 8:42:47 PM] Utkarsh (pushstart): Yes, it is a internal doc to justify that why you had debited your vendor/supplier (on paper), actual conditions may differ.
Yes, it is not legally acceptable so the vendor has to accept that debit note in case to reimburse the taxes levied on that debit note. 
For a given ex, I supplied some stuff to Landmark Group in 2016 and they have debited 3.5 lac from balance due to breakage issues, after mutual understanding I reduced that amount to 2 lac, they raised me a debit note of 2 lac including VAT, I accepted it and reimbursed my 14% taxes from it.
In your case, they havenâ€™t gave you a debit note, so you have a strong side to present to legal authorities.
[05/02/19, 8:51:06 PM] Utkarsh (pushstart): The thing you just mentioned that ordering from someone and not paying him after that is entirely fraudulent techniques and companies who wanted to maintain their market image and value do not indulge in such actions while on other side people who just wanted to make profit from such activities also exist, therefore itâ€™s always recommended to have a PDC from your client in case of any credit period is defined between involving parties.
As updated earlier PDC (Post Dated Cheque) is a guarantee that you can withdraw your agreed amount on specified date, if bounced then there itâ€™s a non-bailable offence.

[07/03/19, 11:38:03 AM] Nidhi Tyagi (ps): *Life of an Entrepreneur!*

When I was an employee I used to think, these employer are so lucky, they have no time restrictions, they can come or leave office anytime and we have to stick to time.

They have no  target given by their bosses, who asks them the status on their performance. Aren't they so happy and free from all these being an employer.

Now let's see it from the different angle,

They can work endlessly for their passion whithout being paid when they start a business.

They have to earn their own salary, no one is there to pay them for their efforts. Even for sometime at early stage the satisfaction of doing what they love is their salary.

They have to give a target to themselves so that they can pay us when we achieve ours.

We can be our own master after office but they are still the master of us all 24Ã—7. There is no working hours limit for them. They are all time working with the concern they carry to grow their business, bring more employement, bringing the funds to paying our next salary, staying strong in competition, dealing with uncertainities, giving themselves a new challenge everyday, new targets that may give them many sleepless nights and much more.

#Entreprenership, being an employer, be your own boss, these terms may look fancy but they are not always so fancy as they look.

Nidhi D Tyagi
www.nidhityagi.com

[08/03/19, 11:56:45 AM] Zain Siddiqui (pushstart): In January of this year, we undertook a week long trip across Rajasthan upto Agra with a couple of friends from around the world. We all went mad clicking epic pictures of each other in every pose one can think of at the forts, in the palaces and all over the streets. And the compelling stories of those places made it all the more epic. However, something hit us a few days after this magical trip was over. 
Rikis said two things about the gullies of India - one, they are so crowded (no surprise) and two, there are very few women in this crowd. 

Now thatâ€™s not something we didnâ€™t know before. Weâ€™ve seen it all our lives. And we even know why it is so!

Why? Why is our country so fucked up? 

So we took Rikisâ€™ observation back to Marol, the home of the Wicked Broz, where weâ€™d been planning a hip hop festival for months. Now, we had a new meaning to it. 

Ladies First is a women-led street art festival. The first of its kind in India. Our endeavour is to promote women street artists and in turn bring more women to the streets in India. Back to the basics, dude! Represent. Hip-hop.

All of us together hope to bring more power to the women on the streets, way beyond the walls of Marol and Mumbai.
